<p><b>William Marsh Rice University</b>, commonly referred to as <b>Rice University</b> or <b>Rice</b>, is a private research university located on a 295-acre (119-hectare) campus in <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. The university is situated near the <a href="/wiki/Houston_Museum_District" title="Houston Museum District">Houston Museum District</a> and is adjacent to the <a href="/wiki/Texas_Medical_Center" title="Texas Medical Center">Texas Medical Center</a>. Rice is generally considered the top university and the most selective institute of higher education in the state of Texas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>Opened in 1912 after the murder of its namesake <a href="/wiki/William_Marsh_Rice" title="William Marsh Rice">William Marsh Rice</a>, Rice is now a research university with an undergraduate focus. Its emphasis on education is demonstrated by a small student body and 6:1 student-faculty ratio.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-At_a_Glance_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-At_a_Glance-3">[3]</a></sup> The university has a very high level of research activity for its size, with $115.3 million in sponsored research funding in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RF_-_Research_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-RF_-_Research-12">[12]</a></sup> Rice is noted for its <a href="/wiki/Applied_science" title="Applied science">applied science</a> programs in the fields of <a href="/wiki/Artificial_heart" title="Artificial heart">artificial heart</a> research, structural chemical analysis, signal processing, space science, and <a href="/wiki/Nanotechnology" title="Nanotechnology">nanotechnology</a>. It was ranked first in the world in <a href="/wiki/Materials_science" title="Materials science">materials science</a> research by the <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education" title="Times Higher Education">Times Higher Education</a> (THE) in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-THE_-_Materials_Science_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-THE_-_Materials_Science-13">[13]</a></sup> Rice is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a>.</p>
<p>The university is organized into eleven <a href="/wiki/Residential_colleges_of_Rice_University" title="Residential colleges of Rice University">residential colleges</a> and eight schools of academic study, including the <a href="/wiki/Wiess_School_of_Natural_Sciences" title="Wiess School of Natural Sciences">Wiess School of Natural Sciences</a>, the <a href="/wiki/George_R._Brown_School_of_Engineering" title="George R. Brown School of Engineering">George R. Brown School of Engineering</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Rice_University_School_of_Social_Sciences" title="Rice University School of Social Sciences">School of Social Sciences</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rice_University_School_of_Architecture" title="Rice University School of Architecture">School of Architecture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shepherd_School_of_Music" title="Shepherd School of Music">Shepherd School of Music</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Rice_University_School_of_Humanities" title="Rice University School of Humanities">School of Humanities</a>. Graduate programs are offered through the <a href="/wiki/Jesse_H._Jones_Graduate_School_of_Business" title="Jesse H. Jones Graduate School of Business">Jesse H. Jones Graduate School of Business</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rice_University_School_of_Architecture" title="Rice University School of Architecture">School of Architecture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shepherd_School_of_Music" title="Shepherd School of Music">Shepherd School of Music</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Susanne_M._Glasscock_School_of_Continuing_Studies" title="Susanne M. Glasscock School of Continuing Studies">Susanne M. Glasscock School of Continuing Studies</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Majors_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Majors-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Degrees_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Degrees-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schools_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Schools-16">[16]</a></sup> Rice students are bound by the strict Honor Code, which is enforced by a student-run Honor Council.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Rice competes in 14 <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I" title="NCAA Division I">NCAA Division I</a> varsity sports and is a part of <a href="/wiki/Conference_USA" title="Conference USA">Conference USA</a>, often competing with its cross-town rival the <a href="/wiki/Houston%E2%80%93Rice_rivalry" title="Houston–Rice rivalry">University of Houston</a>. Intramural and club sports are offered in a wide variety of activities such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazilian_Jiu-Jitsu" title="Brazilian Jiu-Jitsu">jiu jitsu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Water_polo" title="Water polo">water polo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rowing_(sport)" title="Rowing (sport)">crew</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rice_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rice_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:169px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:William_Marsh_Rice.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="238" data-file-width="167" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/59/William_Marsh_Rice.gif" width="167"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:William_Marsh_Rice.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
William Marsh Rice's estate funded the establishment of the Rice Institute</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The history of Rice University began with the untimely demise of Massachusetts businessman <a href="/wiki/William_Marsh_Rice" title="William Marsh Rice">William Marsh Rice</a>, who made his fortune in real estate, railroad development and cotton trading in the state of <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>. In 1891, Rice decided to charter a free-tuition educational institute in Houston, bearing his name, to be created upon his death, earmarking most of his estate towards funding the project. Rice's will specified the institution was to be "a competitive institution of the highest grade" and that only white students would be permitted to attend.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> On the morning of September 23, 1900, Rice, age 84, was found dead by his valet, and presumed to have died in his sleep. Shortly thereafter, a suspiciously large check made out to Rice's New York City lawyer, signed by the late Rice, was noticed by a bank teller due to a misspelling in the recipient's name. The lawyer, <a href="/wiki/Albert_T._Patrick" title="Albert T. Patrick">Albert T. Patrick</a>, then announced that Rice had changed his will to leave the bulk of his fortune to Patrick, rather than to the creation of Rice's educational institute. A subsequent investigation led by the District Attorney of New York resulted in the arrests of Patrick and of Rice's butler and valet Charles F. Jones, who had been persuaded to administer <a href="/wiki/Chloroform" title="Chloroform">chloroform</a> to Rice while he slept. Rice's friend and personal lawyer in Houston, <a href="/wiki/James_A._Baker,_Sr." title="James A. Baker, Sr.">James A. Baker, Sr.</a>, aided in the discovery of what turned out to be a fake will with a forged signature. Jones was not prosecuted since he cooperated with the district attorney, and testified against Patrick. Patrick was found guilty of conspiring to steal Rice's fortune and convicted of murder in 1901, although he was pardoned in 1912 due to conflicting medical testimony.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-poisoner_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-poisoner-19">[19]</a></sup> Baker helped Rice's estate direct the fortune, worth $4.6 million in 1904 ($123 million today), towards the founding of what was to be called the Rice Institute. The board took control of the assets on April 29 of that year.</p>
<p>In 1907, the Board of Trustees selected the head of the Department of Mathematics and Astronomy at <a href="/wiki/Princeton_University" title="Princeton University">Princeton University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Odell_Lovett" title="Edgar Odell Lovett">Edgar Odell Lovett</a>, to head the Institute, which was still in the planning stages. He came recommended by Princeton's president, <a href="/wiki/Woodrow_Wilson" title="Woodrow Wilson">Woodrow Wilson</a>. In 1908, Lovett accepted the challenge, and was formally inaugurated as the Institute's first president on October 12, 1912. Lovett undertook extensive research before formalizing plans for the new Institute, including visits to 78 institutions of higher learning across the world on a long tour between 1908 and 1909. Lovett was impressed by such things as the aesthetic beauty of the uniformity of the architecture at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania" title="University of Pennsylvania">University of Pennsylvania</a>, a theme which was adopted by the Institute, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Residential_college" title="Residential college">residential college</a> system at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cambridge_University" title="Cambridge University">Cambridge University</a> in <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, which was added to the Institute several decades later. Lovett called for the establishment of a university "of the highest grade," "an institution of liberal and technical learning" devoted "quite as much to investigation as to instruction." [We must] "keep the standards up and the numbers down," declared Lovett. "The most distinguished teachers must take their part in undergraduate teaching, and their spirit should dominate it all."</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rice_University_Texas.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="348" data-file-width="599" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Rice_University_Texas.jpg/220px-Rice_University_Texas.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Rice_University_Texas.jpg/330px-Rice_University_Texas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Rice_University_Texas.jpg/440px-Rice_University_Texas.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rice_University_Texas.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rice University</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Establishment_and_growth">Establishment and growth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rice_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Establishment and growth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RiceInstitute1913.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="487" data-file-width="767" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/RiceInstitute1913.png/220px-RiceInstitute1913.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/RiceInstitute1913.png/330px-RiceInstitute1913.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/RiceInstitute1913.png/440px-RiceInstitute1913.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RiceInstitute1913.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An illustration of the Administration Building of Rice University in 1913</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1911 the cornerstone was laid for the Institute's first building, the Administration Building, now known as Lovett Hall in honor of the founding president. On September 23, 1912, the anniversary of William Marsh Rice's murder, the <i>William Marsh Rice Institute for the Advancement of Letters, Science, and Art</i> began course work. 48 male and 29 female students were enrolled, paying no tuition, with classes taught by a dozen faculty. Unusual for the time, Rice accepted coeducational admissions.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Administration_Building,_Rice_Institute,_Houston,_Texas.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="481" data-file-width="747" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Administration_Building%2C_Rice_Institute%2C_Houston%2C_Texas.jpg/220px-Administration_Building%2C_Rice_Institute%2C_Houston%2C_Texas.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Administration_Building%2C_Rice_Institute%2C_Houston%2C_Texas.jpg/330px-Administration_Building%2C_Rice_Institute%2C_Houston%2C_Texas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Administration_Building%2C_Rice_Institute%2C_Houston%2C_Texas.jpg/440px-Administration_Building%2C_Rice_Institute%2C_Houston%2C_Texas.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Administration_Building,_Rice_Institute,_Houston,_Texas.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Administration Building, Rice Institute, Houston, Texas (postcard, circa 1912-1924)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Three weeks after opening, a spectacular international academic festival was held in celebration, bringing Rice to the attention of the entire academic world. Four years later, at the first commencement ceremony, 35 bachelor's degrees and one master's degree were awarded. That year, the student body voted to adopt the Honor System, which still exists today. The first doctorate was conferred in 1918 on mathematician <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Hubert_Evelyn_Bray&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Hubert Evelyn Bray (page does not exist)">Hubert Evelyn Bray</a>.</p>
<p>During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Rice Institute was one of 131 colleges and universities nationally that took part in the <a href="/wiki/V-12_Navy_College_Training_Program" title="V-12 Navy College Training Program">V-12 Navy College Training Program</a> which offered students a path to a Navy commission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-list-of-v-12_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-list-of-v-12-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Founder's Memorial Statue, a bronze statue of a seated William Marsh Rice, holding the original plans for the campus, was dedicated in 1930, and installed in the central academic quad, facing Lovett Hall. The statue was crafted by <a href="/wiki/John_Angel_(sculptor)" title="John Angel (sculptor)">John Angel</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Little_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Little-21">[21]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Residential_college" title="Residential college">residential college</a> system proposed by President Lovett was adopted in 1958, with the East Hall residence becoming <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baker_College_(Rice_University)" title="Baker College (Rice University)">Baker College</a>, South Hall residence becoming <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Will_Rice_College" title="Will Rice College">Will Rice College</a>, West Hall becoming <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hanszen_College" title="Hanszen College">Hanszen College</a>, and the temporary Wiess Hall becoming <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wiess_College" title="Wiess College">Wiess College</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:JFK_at_Rice_University.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="974" data-file-width="1000" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/JFK_at_Rice_University.jpg/170px-JFK_at_Rice_University.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/JFK_at_Rice_University.jpg/255px-JFK_at_Rice_University.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/JFK_at_Rice_University.jpg/340px-JFK_at_Rice_University.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:JFK_at_Rice_University.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
John F. Kennedy speaking at <a href="/wiki/Rice_Stadium_(Rice_University)" title="Rice Stadium (Rice University)">Rice Stadium</a> in 1962</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1959, the <a href="/wiki/Rice_Institute_Computer" title="Rice Institute Computer">Rice Institute Computer</a> went online. 1960 saw Rice Institute formally renamed William Marsh Rice University. Rice acted as a temporary intermediary in the transfer of land between Humble Oil and Refining Company and <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-multiple_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-multiple-22">[22]</a></sup> for the creation of <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>'s Manned Spacecraft Center (now called <a href="/wiki/Johnson_Space_Center" title="Johnson Space Center">Johnson Space Center</a>) in 1962. <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">President John F. Kennedy</a> then made a <a href="/wiki/We_choose_to_go_to_the_Moon" title="We choose to go to the Moon">speech</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasa_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-nasa-23">[23]</a></sup> at <a href="/wiki/Rice_Stadium_(Rice_University)" title="Rice Stadium (Rice University)">Rice Stadium</a> reiterating that the United States intended to reach the moon before the end of the decade of the 1960s, and "to become the world's leading space-faring nation". The relationship of <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> with Rice University and the city of Houston has remained strong to the present day<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Rice_University&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.</p>
<p>The original charter of Rice Institute dictated that the university admit and educate, tuition-free, "the white inhabitants of Houston, and the state of Texas". In 1963, the governing board of Rice University filed a lawsuit to allow the university to modify its charter to admit students of all races and to charge tuition. In 1964, Rice officially amended the university charter to desegregate its graduate and undergraduate divisions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rice1_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-rice1-24">[24]</a></sup> The Trustees of Rice University prevailed in a lawsuit to void the racial language in the trust in 1966.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-university_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-university-25">[25]</a></sup> Rice began charging tuition for the first time in 1965. In the same year, Rice launched a $33 million ($251 million) development campaign. $43 million ($265 million) was raised by its conclusion in 1970. In 1974, two new schools were founded at Rice, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesse_H._Jones_Graduate_School_of_Management" title="Jesse H. Jones Graduate School of Management">Jesse H. Jones Graduate School of Management</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Shepherd_School_of_Music" title="Shepherd School of Music">Shepherd School of Music</a>. The Brown Foundation Challenge, a fund-raising program designed to encourage annual gifts, was launched in 1976 and ended in 1996 having raised $185 million ($283 million). The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rice_School_of_Social_Sciences" title="Rice School of Social Sciences">Rice School of Social Sciences</a> was founded in 1979.</p>
<p>On-campus housing was exclusively for men for the first forty years. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jones_College_(Rice_University)" title="Jones College (Rice University)">Jones College</a> was the first women's residence on the Rice campus, followed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brown_College_(Rice_University)#Brown_College" title="Brown College (Rice University)">Brown College</a>. According to legend, the women's colleges were purposefully situated at the opposite end of campus from the existing men's colleges as a way of preserving campus propriety, which was greatly valued by Edgar Odell Lovett, who did not even allow benches to be installed on campus, fearing that they "might lead to co-fraternization of the sexes".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rice2_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-rice2-26">[26]</a></sup> The path linking the north colleges to the center of campus was given the tongue-in-cheek name of "Virgin's Walk". Individual colleges became coeducational between 1973 and 1987, with the single-sex floors of colleges that had them becoming co-ed by 2006. By then, several new residential colleges had been built on campus to handle the university's growth, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lovett_College" title="Lovett College">Lovett College</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sid_Richardson_College" title="Sid Richardson College">Sid Richardson College</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Martel_College" title="Martel College">Martel College</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_history">Recent history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rice_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Recent history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_in_the_United_States_13-16_November_2001-25.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="334" data-file-width="500" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Vladimir_Putin_in_the_United_States_13-16_November_2001-25.jpg/220px-Vladimir_Putin_in_the_United_States_13-16_November_2001-25.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Vladimir_Putin_in_the_United_States_13-16_November_2001-25.jpg/330px-Vladimir_Putin_in_the_United_States_13-16_November_2001-25.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Vladimir_Putin_in_the_United_States_13-16_November_2001-25.jpg/440px-Vladimir_Putin_in_the_United_States_13-16_November_2001-25.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_in_the_United_States_13-16_November_2001-25.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_H.W._Bush" title="George H.W. Bush">George H.W. Bush</a> meeting <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> at Rice in 2001</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/G8" title="G8">Economic Summit of Industrialized Nations</a> was held at Rice in 1990. In 1993, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_Baker_Institute" title="James Baker Institute">James A. Baker III Institute for Public Policy</a> was created. In 1997, the Edythe Bates Old Grand Organ and Recital Hall and the Center for Nanoscale Science and Technology, renamed in 2005 for the late Nobel Prize winner and Rice professor <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Richard_E._Smalley" title="Richard E. Smalley">Richard E. Smalley</a>, were dedicated at Rice. In 1999, the Center for Biological and Environmental Nanotechnology was created. The <a href="/wiki/Rice_Owls_baseball" title="Rice Owls baseball">Rice Owls baseball</a> team was ranked #1 in the nation for the first time in that year (1999), holding the top spot for eight weeks.</p>
<p>In 2003, the Owls won their first national championship in baseball, which was the first for the university in any team sport, beating Southwest Missouri State in the opening game and then the University of Texas and Stanford University twice each en route to the title. In 2008, President <a href="/wiki/David_Leebron" title="David Leebron">David Leebron</a> issued a ten-point plan titled "Vision for the Second Century" outlining plans to increase research funding, strengthen existing programs, and increase collaboration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vision_for_the_Second_Century_-_Ten_Points_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vision_for_the_Second_Century_-_Ten_Points-27">[27]</a></sup> The plan has brought about another wave of campus constructions, including the erection the newly renamed <a href="/wiki/BioScience_Research_Collaborative" title="BioScience Research Collaborative">BioScience Research Collaborative</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rice3_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-rice3-28">[28]</a></sup> building (intended to foster collaboration with the adjacent <a href="/wiki/Texas_Medical_Center" title="Texas Medical Center">Texas Medical Center</a>), a new recreational center and the renovated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autry_Court" title="Autry Court">Autry Court</a> basketball stadium, and the addition of two new residential colleges, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Duncan_College" title="Duncan College">Duncan College</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/McMurtry_College" title="McMurtry College">McMurtry College</a>.</p>
<p>Beginning in late 2008, the university considered a merger with <a href="/wiki/Baylor_College_of_Medicine" title="Baylor College of Medicine">Baylor College of Medicine</a>, though the merger was ultimately rejected in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ricethresher_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-ricethresher-29">[29]</a></sup> Select Rice undergraduates are currently guaranteed admission to Baylor College of Medicine upon graduation as part of the Rice/Baylor Medical Scholars program. According to History Professor John Boles' recent book <i>University Builder: Edgar Odell Lovett and the Founding of the Rice Institute,</i> the first president's original vision for the university included hopes for future medical and law schools.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus">Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rice_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Campus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Campus_of_Rice_University" title="Campus of Rice University">Campus of Rice University</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rice_University_-_detail.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2448" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Rice_University_-_detail.JPG/220px-Rice_University_-_detail.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Rice_University_-_detail.JPG/330px-Rice_University_-_detail.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Rice_University_-_detail.JPG/440px-Rice_University_-_detail.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rice_University_-_detail.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Herzstein Hall, in the Academic Quad</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Rice's campus is a heavily-wooded 285-acre (115-hectare) tract of land located close to the city of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_University_Place" title="West University Place">West University Place</a>, in the museum district of <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>.</p>
<p>Five streets demarcate the campus: Greenbriar Street, Rice Boulevard, Sunset Boulevard, Main Street, and University Boulevard. For most of its history, all of Rice's buildings have been contained within this "outer loop". In recent years, new facilities have been built close to campus, but the bulk of administrative, academic, and residential buildings are still located within the original pentagonal plot of land. The new Collaborative Research Center, all graduate student housing, the Greenbriar building, and the Wiess President's House are located off-campus.</p>
<p>Rice prides itself on the amount of green space available on campus; there are only about 50 buildings spread between the main entrance at its easternmost corner, and the parking lots and <a href="/wiki/Rice_Stadium_(Rice_University)" title="Rice Stadium (Rice University)">Rice Stadium</a> at the West end. The <a href="/wiki/Lynn_R._Lowrey_Arboretum" title="Lynn R. Lowrey Arboretum">Lynn R. Lowrey Arboretum</a>, consisting of more than 4000 trees and shrubs (giving birth to the legend that Rice has a tree for every student), is spread throughout the campus.</p>
<p>The university's first president, <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Odell_Lovett" title="Edgar Odell Lovett">Edgar Odell Lovett</a>, intended for the campus to have a uniform architecture style to improve its aesthetic appeal. To that end, nearly every building on campus is noticeably <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_architecture" title="Byzantine architecture">Byzantine</a> in style, with sand and pink-colored bricks, large archways and columns being a common theme among many campus buildings. Noteworthy exceptions include the glass-walled Brochstein Pavilion, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lovett_College" title="Lovett College">Lovett College</a> with its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brutalism" title="Brutalism">Brutalist</a>-style concrete gratings, and the eclectic-Mediterranean Duncan Hall. In September 2011, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Travel%2BLeisure" title="Travel+Leisure">Travel+Leisure</a> listed Rice's campus as one of the most beautiful in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>Lovett Hall, named for Rice's visionary first president, is the university's most iconic campus building. Through its Sallyport arch, new students symbolically enter the university during matriculation and depart as graduates at commencement. Duncan Hall, Rice's computational engineering building, was designed to encourage collaboration between the four different departments situated there. The building's colorful Martel Foyer, drawn from many world cultures, was designed by the architect to symbolically express this collaborative purpose.</p>
<p>The campus is organized in a number of <a href="/wiki/Quadrangle_(architecture)" title="Quadrangle (architecture)">quadrangles</a>. The Academic Quad, anchored by a statue of founder <a href="/wiki/William_Marsh_Rice" title="William Marsh Rice">William Marsh Rice</a>, includes <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Adams_Cram" title="Ralph Adams Cram">Ralph Adams Cram</a>'s masterpiece, the asymmetrical Lovett Hall, the original administrative building; Fondren Library; Herzstein Hall, the original physics building and home to the largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amphitheater" title="Amphitheater">amphitheater</a> on campus; Sewall Hall for the social sciences and arts; Rayzor Hall for the languages; and Anderson Hall of the Architecture department. The Humanities Building, winner of several architectural awards, is immediately adjacent to the main quad. Further west lies a quad surrounded by McNair Hall of the <a href="/wiki/Jesse_H._Jones_Graduate_School_of_Business" title="Jesse H. Jones Graduate School of Business">Jones Business School</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_Baker_Institute" title="James Baker Institute">Baker Institute</a>, and Alice Pratt Brown Hall of the <a href="/wiki/Shepherd_School_of_Music" title="Shepherd School of Music">Shepherd School of Music</a>. These two quads are surrounded by the university's main access road, a one-way loop referred to as the "inner loop". In the Engineering Quad, a trinity of sculptures by <a href="/wiki/Michael_Heizer" title="Michael Heizer">Michael Heizer</a>, collectively entitled <i>45 Degrees, 90 Degrees, 180 Degrees</i>, are flanked by Abercrombie Laboratory, the Cox Building, and the Mechanical Laboratory, housing the Electrical, Mechanical, and Earth Science/Civil Engineering departments, respectively. Duncan Hall is the latest addition to this quad, providing new offices for the Computer Science, Computational and Applied Math, Electrical and Computer Engineering, and Statistics departments.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Founders_bench.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1265" data-file-width="1000" height="215" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/71/Founders_bench.jpg/170px-Founders_bench.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/71/Founders_bench.jpg/255px-Founders_bench.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/71/Founders_bench.jpg/340px-Founders_bench.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Founders_bench.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A stone bench in the Academic Quad</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Roughly three-quarters of Rice's undergraduate population lives on campus. Housing is divided among eleven <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Residential_colleges" title="Residential colleges">residential colleges</a>, which form an integral part of student life at the university (see <a href="/wiki/Residential_colleges_of_Rice_University" title="Residential colleges of Rice University">Residential colleges of Rice University</a>). The colleges are named for university historical figures and benefactors, and while there is wide variation in their appearance, facilities, and dates of founding, are an important source of identity for Rice students, functioning as dining halls, residence halls, sports teams, among other roles. Rice does not have or endorse a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greek_system" title="Greek system">Greek system</a>, with the residential college system taking its place. Five colleges, McMurtry, Duncan, Martel, Jones, and Brown are located on the north side of campus, across from the "South Colleges", Baker, Will Rice, Lovett, Hanszen, Sid Richardson, and Wiess, on the other side of the Academic Quadrangle. Of the eleven colleges, Baker is the oldest, originally built in 1912, and the twin Duncan and McMurtry colleges are the newest, and opened for the first time for the 2009-10 school year. Will Rice, Baker, and Lovett colleges are undergoing renovation to expand their dining facilities as well as the number of rooms available for students.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:McNairHall_1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="522" data-file-width="800" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/McNairHall_1.jpg/220px-McNairHall_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/McNairHall_1.jpg/330px-McNairHall_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/McNairHall_1.jpg/440px-McNairHall_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:McNairHall_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
McNair Hall, home to the Jones School of Business</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The on-campus football facility, <a href="/wiki/Rice_Stadium_(Rice_University)" title="Rice Stadium (Rice University)">Rice Stadium</a>, opened in 1950 with a capacity of 70,000 seats. After improvements in 2006, the stadium is currently configured to seat 47,000 for football but can readily be reconfigured to its original capacity of 70,000, more than the total number of Rice alumni, living and deceased.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rice_Official_Athletic_Site_-_Facilities_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rice_Official_Athletic_Site_-_Facilities-31">[31]</a></sup> The stadium was the site of <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_VIII" title="Super Bowl VIII">Super Bowl VIII</a> and a speech by <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a> on September 12, 1962 in which he challenged the nation to send a man to the moon by the end of the decade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rice4_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-rice4-32">[32]</a></sup> The recently renovated <a href="/wiki/Tudor_Fieldhouse" title="Tudor Fieldhouse">Tudor Fieldhouse</a>, formerly known as Autry Court, is home to the basketball and volleyball teams. Other stadia include the <a href="/wiki/Rice_Track/Soccer_Stadium" title="Rice Track/Soccer Stadium">Rice Track/Soccer Stadium</a> and the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jake_Hess_Tennis_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jake Hess Tennis Stadium (page does not exist)">Jake Hess Tennis Stadium</a>. A new Rec Center now houses the intramural sports offices and provide an outdoor pool, training and exercise facilities for all Rice students, while athletics training will solely be held at Tudor Fieldhouse and the Rice Football Stadium.</p>
<p>The university and <a href="/wiki/Houston_Independent_School_District" title="Houston Independent School District">Houston Independent School District</a> jointly established <a href="/wiki/The_Rice_School" title="The Rice School">The Rice School</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Kindergarten" title="Kindergarten">kindergarten</a> through 8th grade public magnet school in Houston.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-houstonisd_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-houstonisd-33">[33]</a></sup> The school opened in August 1994. Through Cy-Fair ISD Rice University offers a credit course based summer school for grades 8 through 12. They also have skills based classes during the summer in the Rice Summer School.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization">Organization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rice_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Organization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sallyport.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4813" data-file-width="3136" height="261" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c6/Sallyport.JPG/170px-Sallyport.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c6/Sallyport.JPG/255px-Sallyport.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c6/Sallyport.JPG/340px-Sallyport.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sallyport.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Students walk through the Sallyport upon matriculation and commencement</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Rice University is chartered as a non-profit organization and is governed by a privately appointed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Board_of_trustees" title="Board of trustees">board of trustees</a>. The board consists of a maximum of 25 voting members who serve four-year terms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Handbook_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Handbook-34">[34]</a></sup> The trustees serve without compensation and a simple majority of trustees must reside in Texas, including at least 4 within the greater Houston area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Handbook_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-Handbook-34">[34]</a></sup> The board of trustees delegates its power by appointing a President to serve as the chief executive of the university. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/David_W._Leebron" title="David W. Leebron">David W. Leebron</a> was appointed President in 2004 and succeeded <a href="/wiki/S._Malcolm_Gillis" title="S. Malcolm Gillis">Malcolm Gillis</a> who served since 1993. The provost, six vice presidents, and other university officials report to the President. The President is advised by a University Council composed of the Provost, eight members of the Faculty Council, two staff members, one graduate student, and two undergraduate students. The President presides over a Faculty Council which has the authority to alter curricular requirements, establish new degree programs, and approve candidates for degrees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Handbook_34-2"><a href="#cite_note-Handbook-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<table style="border:1px solid #ddd; background:#fefefe; padding:3px; margin:0;">
<tr>
<td>
<p>Undergraduate and Graduate Schools</p>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Rice_University_School_of_Architecture" title="Rice University School of Architecture">Rice University School of Architecture</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/George_R._Brown_School_of_Engineering" title="George R. Brown School of Engineering">George R. Brown School of Engineering</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Rice_University_School_of_Humanities" title="Rice University School of Humanities">School of Humanities</a></li>

<li>The <a href="/wiki/Wiess_School_of_Natural_Sciences" title="Wiess School of Natural Sciences">Wiess School of Natural Sciences</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Rice_University_School_of_Social_Sciences" title="Rice University School of Social Sciences">Rice University School of Social Sciences</a></li>
</ul>
</td>
<td style="width:40px;"></td>

<p>Graduate Schools</p>
<ul>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesse_H._Jones_Graduate_School_of_Management" title="Jesse H. Jones Graduate School of Management">Jesse H. Jones Graduate School of Management</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Susanne_M._Glasscock_School_of_Continuing_Studies" title="Susanne M. Glasscock School of Continuing Studies">Susanne M. Glasscock School of Continuing Studies</a></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Rice's undergraduate students benefit from a centralized admissions process, which admits new students to the university as a whole, rather than a specific school (the schools of Music and Architecture are decentralized). Students are encouraged to select the major path that best suits their desires; a student can later decide that they would rather pursue study in another field, or continue their current coursework and add a second or third major. These transitions are designed to be simple at Rice, with students not required to decide on a specific major until their sophomore year of study.</p>
<p>Rice's academics are organized into six schools which offer courses of study at the graduate and undergraduate level, with two more being primarily focused on graduate education, while offering select opportunities for undergraduate students. Rice offers 360 degrees in over 60 departments. There are 40 undergraduate degree programs, 51 masters programs, and 29 doctoral programs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Majors_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-Majors-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Degrees_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-Degrees-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Undergraduate tuition for the 2011-2012 school year is $34,900. $651 is charged for fees, and Rice projects an $800 budget for books and $1550 for personal expenses. Rice students are charged $12,270 for room and board. Per year, the total cost of a Rice University education is $50,171.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RF-Students_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-RF-Students-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Faculty members of each of the departments elect chairs to represent the department to each School's dean and the deans report to the Provost who serves as the chief officer for academic affairs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Handbook_34-3"><a href="#cite_note-Handbook-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rice_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lovett_Hall.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="492" data-file-width="800" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Lovett_Hall.jpg/220px-Lovett_Hall.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Lovett_Hall.jpg/330px-Lovett_Hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Lovett_Hall.jpg/440px-Lovett_Hall.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lovett_Hall.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lovett Hall, formerly known as the Administration Building, was the first building on campus</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Rice is a medium-sized, highly residential research university.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carnegie_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie-36">[36]</a></sup> The majority of enrollments are in the full-time, four-year undergraduate program emphasizing arts &amp; sciences and professions. There is a high graduate coexistence with the comprehensive graduate program and a very high level of research activity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carnegie_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie-36">[36]</a></sup> It is accredited by the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Association_of_Colleges_and_Schools" title="Southern Association of Colleges and Schools">Southern Association of Colleges and Schools</a> as well as the professional accreditation agencies for engineering, management, and architecture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rice_Facts_-_University_Accreditation_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rice_Facts_-_University_Accreditation-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>Each of Rice's departments is organized into one of three distribution groups, and students whose major lies within the scope of one group must take at least 12 credit hours of approved distribution classes in each of the other two groups, as well as completing one physical education course as part of the LPAP (Lifetime Physical Activity Program) requirement. All new students must take a Freshman Writing Intensive Seminar (FWIS) class, and for students who do not pass the university's writing composition examination (administered during the summer before matriculation), FWIS 100, a writing class, becomes an additional requirement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>The majority of Rice's undergraduate degree programs grant B.S. or B.A. degrees. Rice has recently begun to offer minors in areas such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesse_H._Jones_Graduate_School_of_Management" title="Jesse H. Jones Graduate School of Management">business</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rice5_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-rice5-39">[39]</a></sup> energy and water sustainability,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rice_University_Department_of_Sociology_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rice_University_Department_of_Sociology-40">[40]</a></sup> and global health.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beyond_Traditional_Borders_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-Beyond_Traditional_Borders-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_body">Student body</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rice_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Student body">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p>Women make up 48% of the undergraduate body and 36% of the professional and post-graduate student body as of fall 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDS2014-B_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-CDS2014-B-42">[42]</a></sup> The student body consists of students from all 50 states, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/District_of_Columbia" title="District of Columbia">District of Columbia</a>, two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Incorporated_territory#Classification_of_current_U.S._territories" title="Incorporated territory">U.S. Territories</a>, and 83 foreign countries.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Forty percent of degree-seeking students are from Texas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Honor_Code">Honor Code</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rice_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Honor Code">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Rice Honor Code plays an integral role in academic affairs. Almost all Rice exams are unproctored and professors give timed, closed-book exams that students take home and complete at their own convenience. Potential infractions are reported to the student Honor Council, elected by popular vote. The penalty structure is established every year by Council consensus; typically, penalties have ranged from a letter of reprimand to an 'F' in the course and a two semester suspension.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rice_Honor_Council_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rice_Honor_Council-45">[45]</a></sup> During Orientation Week, students must take and pass a test demonstrating that they understand the Honor System's requirements and sign a Matriculation Pledge. On assignments, students affirm their commitment to the Honor Code by writing <i>On my honor, I have neither given nor received any unauthorized aid on this (examination, quiz or paper).</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research_centers_and_resources">Research centers and resources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rice_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Research centers and resources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Rice is noted for its pioneer <a href="/wiki/Applied_science" title="Applied science">applied science</a> programs in the fields of <a href="/wiki/Nanotechnology" title="Nanotechnology">nanotechnology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Artificial_heart" title="Artificial heart">artificial heart</a> research, structural chemical analysis, and <a href="/wiki/Outline_of_space_science" title="Outline of space science">space science</a>, being ranked 1st in the world in <a href="/wiki/Materials_science" title="Materials science">materials science</a> research by the Times Higher Education (THE) in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Top_institutions_in_materials_science_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-Top_institutions_in_materials_science-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Richard E. Smalley Institute for Nanoscale Science and Technology (Smalley Institute)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Richard_E._Smalley_Institute_for_Nanoscale_Science_and_Technology_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Richard_E._Smalley_Institute_for_Nanoscale_Science_and_Technology-47">[47]</a></sup> - the nation's first nanotechnology center</li>
<li>Center for Biological and Environmental Nanotechnology (CBEN)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CBEN_Center_for_Biological_and_Environmental_Nanotechnology_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-CBEN_Center_for_Biological_and_Environmental_Nanotechnology-48">[48]</a></sup> - promotes the discovery and development of nanomaterials that enable new medical and environmental technologies</li>
<li>Laboratory for Nanophotonics (LANP)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-L_A_N_P_:_Laboratory_for_Nanophotonics_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-L_A_N_P_:_Laboratory_for_Nanophotonics-49">[49]</a></sup> - provides a resource for education and research breakthroughs and advances in the broad, multidisciplinary field of nanophotonics</li>
<li>Digital Signal Processing (DSP)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Digital_Signal_Processing_at_Rice_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Digital_Signal_Processing_at_Rice-50">[50]</a></sup> - center for education and research in the field of digital signal processing</li>
<li>Rice Quantum Institute<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rice_Quantum_Institute_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rice_Quantum_Institute-51">[51]</a></sup> - organization dedicated to research and higher education in areas relating to quantum phenomena</li>
<li>Rice Space Institute<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RSI_Rice_Space_Institute_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-RSI_Rice_Space_Institute-52">[52]</a></sup> -fosters programs in all areas of space research</li>
<li>Institute of Biosciences and Bioengineering (IBB)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rice6_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-rice6-53">[53]</a></sup> - facilitates the translation of interdisciplinary research and education in biosciences and bioengineering</li>
<li>Ken Kennedy Institute for Information Technology<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rice7_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-rice7-54">[54]</a></sup> - dedicated to the advancement of applied interdisciplinary research in the areas of computation and information technology</li>
<li>Baker Institute for Public Policy<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bakerinstitute_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-bakerinstitute-55">[55]</a></sup> - one of the leading nonpartisan public policy think-tanks in the country</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/OpenStax_CNX" title="OpenStax CNX">OpenStax CNX</a> (formerly <i>Connexions</i>) and <a href="/wiki/OpenStax_College" title="OpenStax College">OpenStax College</a> - an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Open_source" title="Open source">open source</a> platform and <a href="/wiki/Open_access" title="Open access">open access</a> publisher, respectively, of <a href="/wiki/Open_educational_resources" title="Open educational resources">open educational resources</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rice_Alliance_for_Technology_and_Entrepreneurship" title="Rice Alliance for Technology and Entrepreneurship">Rice Alliance for Technology and Entrepreneurship</a> - supports entrepreneurs and early-stage technology ventures in Houston and Texas through education, collaboration, and research, ranked No. 1 among top university business incubators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mid-InfraRed_Technologies_for_Health_and_the_Environment" title="Mid-InfraRed Technologies for Health and the Environment">Mid-InfraRed Technologies for Health and the Environment</a> (MIRTHE)</li>
<li>Rice Gallery<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rice_Gallery.2C_Houston.2C_Texas_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rice_Gallery.2C_Houston.2C_Texas-57">[57]</a></sup></li>
<li>Kinder Institute for Urban Research - conducts the Houston Area Survey, "the nation's longest running study of any metropolitan region's economy, population, life experiences, beliefs and attitudes" <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></li>
<li>Humanities Research Center (HRC) - identifies, encourages, and funds innovative research projects by faculty, visiting scholars, graduate, and undergraduate students in the School of Humanities and beyond<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></li>
<li>Center for the Study of Women, Gender, and Sexuality (CSWGS)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></li>
<li>Rice Center for Critical and Cultural Theory (3CT) - promotes intellectual synergy and community among Rice faculty and graduate students whose work is informed by a deep and sustained engagement with critical and cultural theory and their ongoing development and permutations<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></li>
<li>Chao Center for Asian Studies<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Admissions">Admissions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rice_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Admissions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="wikitable" style="float:right; font-size:85%; margin:10px">
<caption><i>Fall Freshman Statistics</i></caption>
<tr>

<p>Admission to Rice is rated as "most selective" by <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>For fall 2015, Rice received 17,951 freshmen applications; 2,865 were admitted (16.0%) and 969 enrolled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDS2015_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-CDS2015-64">[64]</a></sup> The middle 50% range of <a href="/wiki/SAT" title="SAT">SAT</a> scores were 680-760 for critical reading, 710-800 for math, and 680-770 for writing; the middle 50% range of the <a href="/wiki/ACT_(test)" title="ACT (test)">ACT</a> Composite score was 32-35.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDS2015_64-2"><a href="#cite_note-CDS2015-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
