<p>In 2016, Rice was ranked 87th in the world by the <i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a></i>. In 2016, Rice was ranked tied for 72nd internationally (38th nationally) by the <i><a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a></i>. Rice University was also ranked 90th globally in 2016 by <i><a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a></i>. Rice is noted for its entrepreneurial activity, and has been recognized as the top ranked <a href="/wiki/Business_incubator" title="Business incubator">business incubator</a> in the world by the <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a>-based <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=UBI_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="UBI Index (page does not exist)">UBI Index</a> for both 2013 and 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>Rice was ranked tied at 15th among national universities and at 5th for "best undergraduate teaching" in the U.S. by <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i> in its 2017 edition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USNWR_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-USNWR-77">[77]</a></sup> <i>USNWR</i> also ranked the Jones Graduate School of Management tied for 33rd and the Brown School of Engineering 31st in the nation in 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USNWR_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-USNWR-77">[77]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> magazine ranked Rice University at 30th nationally among both liberal arts colleges and universities in 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Kiplinger%27s_Personal_Finance" title="Kiplinger's Personal Finance">Kiplinger's Personal Finance</a></i> places Rice 4th in its 2015 ranking of best value private universities in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Princeton_Review" title="Princeton Review">Princeton Review</a></i> ranked Rice 1st for "Best Quality of Life" and "Happiest Students" in its 2012 edition,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rice_University_-_Rankings_.26_Lists_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rice_University_-_Rankings_.26_Lists-80">[80]</a></sup> 20th among <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">LGBT</a> friendliest colleges in its 2014 edition,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> and one of the top 50 best value private colleges in its 2011 edition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rice_University_-_Rankings_.26_Lists8_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rice_University_-_Rankings_.26_Lists8-82">[82]</a></sup> Rice was ranked 41st among research universities by the Center for Measuring University Performance in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Top_American_Research_Universities_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Top_American_Research_Universities-83">[83]</a></sup> <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Consumer%27s_Digest" title="Consumer's Digest">Consumer's Digest</a></i> ranked Rice 3rd on the list of top 5 values in private colleges in its June 2011 issue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rice9_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-rice9-84">[84]</a></sup> <i>Fiske Guide to Colleges</i> ranked Rice as one of the top 25 private "best buy" schools in its 2012 edition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rice_a_best_buy_in_2012_Fiske_college_guide_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rice_a_best_buy_in_2012_Fiske_college_guide-85">[85]</a></sup> In 2011 the <a href="/wiki/CWTS_Leiden_Ranking" title="CWTS Leiden Ranking">Leiden Ranking</a>, which measures the performance of 500 major research universities worldwide, using metrics designed to measure research impact ranked Rice 4th Globally, for effectiveness and contribution of research.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rice10_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-rice10-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leiden_Ranking_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Leiden_Ranking-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leidenranking_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-leidenranking-88">[88]</a></sup> In 2013 the university was again ranked first globally for quality of research in natural sciences and engineering, and 6th globally for all sciences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> In 2014, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Beast" title="The Daily Beast">The Daily Beast</a></i> ranked Rice 14th out of nearly 2,000 schools it evaluated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> In 2016, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Money_Magazine" title="Money Magazine">Money Magazine</a></i> ranked Rice 4th in the nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rice_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rice_University_-_Arboretum.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Rice_University_-_Arboretum.JPG/220px-Rice_University_-_Arboretum.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Rice_University_-_Arboretum.JPG/330px-Rice_University_-_Arboretum.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Rice_University_-_Arboretum.JPG/440px-Rice_University_-_Arboretum.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rice_University_-_Arboretum.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A view along the inner loop, with three of the university service personnel's traditional golf carts in view</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Situated on nearly 300 acres (120 ha) in the heart of Houston's Museum District and across the street from the city's Hermann Park, Rice is a green and leafy refuge – an oasis of learning convenient to the amenities of the nation's fourth-largest city. Rice's campus adjoins <a href="/wiki/Hermann_Park" title="Hermann Park">Hermann Park</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Texas_Medical_Center" title="Texas Medical Center">Texas Medical Center</a>, and a neighborhood commercial center called <a href="/wiki/Rice_Village" title="Rice Village">Rice Village</a>. Hermann Park includes the <a href="/wiki/Houston_Museum_of_Natural_Science" title="Houston Museum of Natural Science">Houston Museum of Natural Science</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Houston_Zoo" title="Houston Zoo">Houston Zoo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miller_Outdoor_Theatre" title="Miller Outdoor Theatre">Miller Outdoor Theatre</a> and an 18-hole municipal golf course. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reliant_Park" title="Reliant Park">Reliant Park</a>, home of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reliant_Stadium" title="Reliant Stadium">Reliant Stadium</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Astrodome" title="Astrodome">Astrodome</a>, is two miles (3 km) south of the campus. Among the dozen or so museums in the <a href="/wiki/Houston_Museum_District" title="Houston Museum District">Museum District</a> is the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Rice_University_Art_Gallery&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Rice University Art Gallery (page does not exist)">Rice University Art Gallery</a>, open during the school year. Easy access to downtown's theater and nightlife district and to Reliant Park is provided by the Houston <a href="/wiki/METRORail" title="METRORail">METRORail</a> system, with a station adjacent to the campus's main gate. The campus recently joined the <a href="/wiki/Zipcar" title="Zipcar">Zipcar</a> program with two vehicles to increase the transportation options for students and staff who need but currently don't utilize a vehicle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rice11_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-rice11-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Residential_colleges">Residential colleges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rice_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Residential colleges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Residential_colleges_of_Rice_University" title="Residential colleges of Rice University">Residential colleges of Rice University</a></div>
<p>In 1957, Rice University implemented a <a href="/wiki/Residential_college" title="Residential college">residential college</a> system, as proposed by the university's first president, <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Odell_Lovett" title="Edgar Odell Lovett">Edgar Odell Lovett</a>. The system was inspired by existing systems in place at <a href="/wiki/Oxbridge" title="Oxbridge">Oxford and Cambridge</a> in England and at several other universities in the United States, most notably <a href="/wiki/Residential_colleges_of_Yale_University" title="Residential colleges of Yale University">Yale University</a>. The existing residences known as East, South, West, and Wiess Halls became Baker, Will Rice, Hanszen, and Wiess Colleges, respectively.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_residential_colleges">List of residential colleges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rice_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: List of residential colleges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>This is a list of residential colleges at Rice:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rice12_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-rice12-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<ol>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baker_College_(Rice_University)" title="Baker College (Rice University)">Baker College</a>, named in honor of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Captain_James_A._Baker" title="Captain James A. Baker">Captain James A. Baker</a>, friend and attorney of <a href="/wiki/William_Marsh_Rice" title="William Marsh Rice">William Marsh Rice</a>, and first chair of the Rice Board of Governors.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brown_College_(Rice_University)" title="Brown College (Rice University)">Brown College</a>, named for Margaret Root Brown by her in-laws, <a href="/wiki/George_R._Brown" title="George R. Brown">George R. Brown</a>.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Duncan_College_(Rice_University)" title="Duncan College (Rice University)">Duncan College</a>, named for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charles_Duncan,_Jr." title="Charles Duncan, Jr.">Charles Duncan, Jr.</a>, Secretary of Energy.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hanszen_College_(Rice_University)" title="Hanszen College (Rice University)">Hanszen College</a>, named for Harry Clay Hanszen, benefactor to the university and chairman of the Rice Board of Governors from 1946-1950.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jones_College_(Rice_University)" title="Jones College (Rice University)">Jones College</a>, named for Mary Gibbs Jones, wife of prominent Houston philanthropist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesse_Holman_Jones" title="Jesse Holman Jones">Jesse Holman Jones</a>.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lovett_College_(Rice_University)" title="Lovett College (Rice University)">Lovett College</a>, named after the university's first president, Edgar Odell Lovett.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Martel_College_(Rice_University)" title="Martel College (Rice University)">Martel College</a>, named for Marian and Speros P. Martel, was built in 2002.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/McMurtry_College_(Rice_University)" title="McMurtry College (Rice University)">McMurtry College</a>, named for Rice alumni Burt and Deedee McMurtry, <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Valley" title="Silicon Valley">Silicon Valley</a> venture capitalists.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sid_Richardson_College_(Rice_University)" title="Sid Richardson College (Rice University)">Sid Richardson College</a>, named for the Sid Richardson Foundation, which was established by Texas oilman, cattleman, and philanthropist <a href="/wiki/Sid_W._Richardson" title="Sid W. Richardson">Sid W. Richardson</a>.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wiess_College_(Rice_University)" title="Wiess College (Rice University)">Wiess College</a>, named for Harry Carothers Wiess (1887–1948), one of the founders and one-time president of <a href="/wiki/Humble_Oil" title="Humble Oil">Humble Oil</a>, now <a href="/wiki/ExxonMobil" title="ExxonMobil">ExxonMobil</a>.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Will_Rice_College_(Rice_University)" title="Will Rice College (Rice University)">Will Rice College</a>, named for William M. Rice, Jr., the nephew of the university's founder, <a href="/wiki/William_Marsh_Rice" title="William Marsh Rice">William Marsh Rice</a>.</li>
</ol>
<p>Although each college is composed of a full cross-section of students at Rice, they have over time developed their own traditions and "personalities". When students <a href="/wiki/Matriculation" title="Matriculation">matriculate</a> they are randomly assigned to one of the eleven colleges, although "legacy" exceptions are made for students whose siblings or other close relatives have attended Rice. Students generally remain members of the college that they are assigned to for the duration of their undergraduate careers, even if they move off-campus at any point. Students are guaranteed on-campus housing for freshman year and two of the next three years; each college has its own system for determining allocation of the remaining spaces, collectively known as "Room Jacking". Students develop strong loyalties to their college and maintain friendly rivalry with other colleges, especially during events such as <a href="#Beer_Bike_Race">Beer Bike Race</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orientation_week" title="Orientation week">O-Week</a>. Colleges keep their rivalries alive by performing "jacks," or pranks, on each other, especially during O-Week and <a href="#Beer_Bike_Race">Willy Week</a>. During Matriculation, Commencement, and other formal academic ceremonies, the colleges process in the order in which they were established.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditions">Traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rice_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Traditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Baker_13">Baker 13</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rice_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Baker 13">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Baker 13 is a tradition in which students run around campus wearing nothing but shoes and <a href="/wiki/Shaving_cream" title="Shaving cream">shaving cream</a> at 10 p.m. on the 13th and the 31st of every month (the 26th on months with fewer than 31 days). The event, long sponsored by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baker_College_(Rice_University)" title="Baker College (Rice University)">Baker College</a>, usually attracts a small number of students, but <a href="/wiki/Halloween" title="Halloween">Halloween</a> night and the first and last relevant days of the school year both attract large numbers of revelers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rice_undergrads_share_a_sense_of_community_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rice_undergrads_share_a_sense_of_community-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Beer_Bike_Race">Beer Bike Race</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rice_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Beer Bike Race">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>According to the official <a class="external text" href="http://rpc.rice.edu/beer-bike/" rel="nofollow">website</a>: "Beer Bike is a combination intramural bicycle race and drinking competition dating back to 1957. Ten riders and ten chuggers make up a team. Elaborate rules include details such as a prohibition of "bulky or wet clothing articles designed to absorb beer/water or prevent spilled beer/water from being seen" and regulations for chug can design. Each residential college as well as the Graduate Student Association participates with a men's team, a women's team, and alumni (co-ed) team. Each leg of the race is a relay in which a team's "chugger" must chug 24 US fluid ounces (710 ml) of beer or water for the men's division and 12 US fluid ounces (350 ml) for women before the team's "rider" may begin to ride.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beer_Bike.27s_50th_bash_lets_good_time_roll_at_Rice:_tradition_that_began_in_1957_now_integral_part_of_school.27s_social_scene_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-Beer_Bike.27s_50th_bash_lets_good_time_roll_at_Rice:_tradition_that_began_in_1957_now_integral_part_of_school.27s_social_scene-95">[95]</a></sup> Participants who both ride and chug are referred to as "Ironmen". Willy Week is a term coined in the 1990s to refer to the week preceding Beer-Bike, a time of general energy and excitement on campus. Jacks (pranks) are especially common during Willy Week; some examples in the past include removing showerheads and encasing the Hanszen guardian." The morning of the Beer Bike race itself begins with what is by some estimations the largest annual water balloon fight in the world. Beer-Bike is Rice's most prominent student event, and for younger alumni it serves as an unofficial reunion weekend on par with Homecoming. The 2009 Beer Bike race was dedicated to the memory of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/William_L._Wilson_(Rice_University)" title="William L. Wilson (Rice University)">Dr. Bill Wilson</a>, a popular professor and long-time resident associate of Wiess College who died earlier that year.</p>
<p>In the event of inclement weather, Beer Bike becomes a Beer Run. The rules are nearly identical, except that the Bikers must instead run the length of the track. The most recent Beer Run occurred in 2016.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus_institutions">Campus institutions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rice_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Campus institutions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A number of on-campus institutions form an integral part of student life at Rice. Many of these organizations have been operating for several decades.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rice_Coffeehouse">Rice Coffeehouse</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rice_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Rice Coffeehouse">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Rice Coffeehouse finds its beginnings in Hanszen College, where students would serve coffee in the Weenie Loft - a study room in the old section's fourth floor. Later, the coffee house moved to the Hanszen basement to accommodate more student patrons. That coffeehouse became known as Breadsticks and Pomegranates. Due to flooding, an unfortunate effect of 1) its location in the basement and 2) the Houston climate, this coffee house closed. Demand for an on-campus Coffeehouse grew and in 1990, the Rice Coffeehouse was founded.</p>
<p>The Rice Coffeehouse is a not-for-profit student-run organization serving Rice University and the greater Houston community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Coffeehouse:_16_Years_of_Providing_Rice_with_Society.27s_Most_Acceptable_Drug_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-Coffeehouse:_16_Years_of_Providing_Rice_with_Society.27s_Most_Acceptable_Drug-96">[96]</a></sup> Over the past few years,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (October 2010)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> it has introduced fair-trade and organic coffee and loose-leaf teas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>Coffeehouse baristas are referred to as K.O.C.'s, or Keepers of the Coffee. Rice Coffeehouse has also adopted an unofficial mascot, the squirrel, which can be found on T-shirts, mugs, and bumper stickers stuck on laptops across campus. The logo pays tribute to Rice's unusually plump and frighteningly tame squirrel population.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Valhalla">Valhalla</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rice_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Valhalla">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Valhalla is a non-profit graduate student pub located under Keck Hall which serves as the social nexus for graduate student life at Rice, and the pub is primarily staffed and managed by volunteer Rice graduate students.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Valhalla:_Mythical_Beings_and_Cheap_Beer_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-Valhalla:_Mythical_Beings_and_Cheap_Beer-98">[98]</a></sup> The pub's patrons have expanded beyond graduate students and other members of the local community in recent years, and the pub has become a regular on the annual "Best of Houston" published by the <i><a href="/wiki/Houston_Press" title="Houston Press">Houston Press</a></i>, being named the "Best Place to Meet Single Women" in 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Houston_-_Best_Of_-_Best_Place_to_Meet_Single_Women_-_.282004.29_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-Houston_-_Best_Of_-_Best_Place_to_Meet_Single_Women_-_.282004.29-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Willy.27s_Pub">Willy's Pub</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rice_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Willy's Pub">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Willy's Pub is Rice's undergraduate pub run by students located in the basement of the Rice Memorial Center. It opened on April 11, 1975, with Rice President Norman Hackerman pouring the first beer. The name was chosen by students in tribute to the university's founder, <a href="/wiki/William_Marsh_Rice" title="William Marsh Rice">William Marsh Rice</a>. After the drinking age in Texas was raised in 1986, the pub entered a period of financial difficulties and in April 1995, was destroyed in a fire. The space was gutted but renovated and remains open.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Willy.27s_Pub_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-Willy.27s_Pub-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Willy.27s_Pub.2C_1975_-_1995_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-Willy.27s_Pub.2C_1975_-_1995-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rice_Bikes">Rice Bikes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rice_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Rice Bikes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Rice Bikes is Rice's newest student-run business. They function as a full-service on-campus bicycle store, rental shop, and repair shop. It originated in the basement of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sid_Richardson_College" title="Sid Richardson College">Sid Richardson College</a> in February 2011. In spring 2012, it officially became the third student-run business. A group of students in a <a href="/wiki/Sociology" title="Sociology">sociology</a> class at Rice started a bicycle rental business, and in fall 2013 it and Rice Bikes merged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> It is now located in the Rice Memorial Center.</p>
<p>Rice Bikes sells refurbished bicycles bought from students and functions as a full bicycle repair shop.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Student-run_media">Student-run media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rice_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Student-run media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Rice has a weekly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Student_newspaper" title="Student newspaper">student newspaper</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Rice_Thresher" title="Rice Thresher">The Rice Thresher</a></i>), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/College_radio" title="College radio">college radio</a> station (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KTRU_Rice_Radio" title="KTRU Rice Radio">KTRU Rice Radio</a>), and campus-wide <a href="/wiki/Student_television_station" title="Student television station">student television station</a> (RTV5). All three are based out of the RMC student center. In addition, Rice hosts several student magazines dedicated to a range of different topics; in fact, the spring semester of 2008 saw the birth of two such magazines, a literary sex journal called <i>Open</i> and an undergraduate science research magazine entitled <i>Catalyst</i>.</p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Rice_Thresher" title="Rice Thresher">The Rice Thresher</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ricethresher13_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-ricethresher13-104">[104]</a></sup> is published every Wednesday and is ranked by Princeton Review as one of the top campus newspapers nationally for student readership. It is distributed around campus, and at a few other local businesses and has a website. The <i>Thresher</i> has a small, dedicated staff and is known for its coverage of campus news, open submission opinion page, and the satirical Backpage, which has often been the center of controversy. The newspaper has won several awards at Associated Collegiate Press conferences.</p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KTRU_Rice_Radio" title="KTRU Rice Radio">KTRU Rice Radio</a> is the student-run radio station. Though most DJs are Rice students, anyone is allowed to apply. It is known for playing genres and artists of music and sound unavailable on other radio stations in Houston, and often, the US. The station takes requests over the phone or <a class="external text" href="http://ktru.org/e-quest" rel="nofollow">online</a>. In 2000 and 2006, KTRU won Houston Press' Best Radio Station in Houston.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Houston_Best_of_Houston_-_Best_Radio_Station_-_page_1_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-Houston_Best_of_Houston_-_Best_Radio_Station_-_page_1-105">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Houston_-_Best_of_Houston_-_Houston_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-Houston_-_Best_of_Houston_-_Houston-106">[106]</a></sup> In 2003, Rice alum and active KTRU DJ DL's hip-hip show won Houston Press' Best Hip-hop Radio Show.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Houston_Best_of_Houston_-_Best_Hip-hop_Radio_Show_-_page_1_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-Houston_Best_of_Houston_-_Best_Hip-hop_Radio_Show_-_page_1-107">[107]</a></sup> On August 17, 2010, it was announced that Rice University had been in negotiations to sell the station's broadcast tower, FM frequency and license to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Houston_System" title="University of Houston System">University of Houston System</a> to become a full-time <a href="/wiki/Classical_music" title="Classical music">classical music</a> and fine arts programming station. The new station, <a href="/wiki/KXNG" title="KXNG">KUHA</a>, would be operated as a not-for-profit outlet with listener supporters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sale1_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-sale1-108">[108]</a></sup> The FCC approved the sale and granted the transfer of license to the University of Houston System on April 15, 2011,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Correspondence_for_KTRU_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-Correspondence_for_KTRU-109">[109]</a></sup> however, KUHA proved to be an even larger failure and so after four and a half years of operation, The University of Houston System announced that KUHA's broadcast tower, FM frequency and license were once again up for sale in August 2015. KTRU continued to operate much as it did previously, streaming live on the Internet, via apps, and on HD2 radio using the 90.1 signal. Under student leadership, KTRU explored the possibility of returning to FM radio for a number of years. In spring 2015, KTRU was granted permission by the FCC to begin development of a new broadcast signal via LPFM radio. On October 1, 2015, KTRU made its official return to FM radio on the 96.1 signal. While broadcasting on HD2 radio has been discontinued, KTRU continues to broadcast via internet in addition to its LPFM signal.</p>
<p>RTV5 is a student-run television network available as channel 5 on campus. RTV5 was created initially as Rice Broadcast Television in 1997; RBT began to broadcast the following year in 1998, and aired its first live show across campus in 1999. It experienced much growth and exposure over the years with successful programs like "Drinking with Phil," a weekly news show, and extensive live coverage in December 2000 of the shut down of KTRU by the administration. In spring 2001, the Rice undergraduate community voted in the general elections to support RBT as a blanket tax organization, effectively providing a yearly income of $10,000 to purchase new equipment and provide the campus with a variety of new programming. In the spring of 2005, RBT members decided the station needed a new image and a new name: Rice Television 5. The station has recently set about revitalizing its staff roster and campus image; one of RTV5's most popular shows is the 24-hour show, where a camera and couch placed in the RMC stay on air for 24 hours. One such show is held in fall and another in spring, usually during a weekend allocated for visits by prospective students. RTV5 has a video on demand site at rtv5.rice.edu.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rice14_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-rice14-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>The Rice Review</i>, also known as R2, is a yearly student-run literary journal at Rice University that publishes prose, poetry, and creative nonfiction written by undergraduate students, as well as interviews. The journal was founded in 2004 by creative writing professor and author <a href="/wiki/Justin_Cronin" title="Justin Cronin">Justin Cronin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rice15_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-rice15-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>The Rice Standard</i> is an independent, student-run variety magazine modeled after such publications as <i>The New Yorker</i> and <i>Harper's</i>. Prior to fall 2009, it was regularly published three times a semester with a wide array of content, running from analyses of current events and philosophical pieces to personal essays, short fiction and poetry. In August 2009, the <i>Standard</i> transitioned to a completely online format with the launch of their redesigned website, ricestandard.org. The first website of its kind on Rice's campus, the <i>Standard</i> now features blog-style content written by and for Rice students. <i>The Rice Standard</i> has around 20 regular contributors, and the site features new content every day (including holidays).</p>
<p><i>Open</i>, a magazine dedicated to "literary sex content," predictably caused a stir on campus with its initial publication in spring 2008. A mixture of essays, editorials, stories and artistic photography brought Open attention both on campus and in the <a href="/wiki/Houston_Chronicle" title="Houston Chronicle">Houston Chronicle</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chron_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-chron-112">[112]</a></sup> The third and last annual edition of <i>Open</i> was released in spring of 2010.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rice_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rice_Owls" title="Rice Owls">Rice Owls</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rice_University_Stadium.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1662" data-file-width="1186" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Rice_University_Stadium.jpg/170px-Rice_University_Stadium.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Rice_University_Stadium.jpg/255px-Rice_University_Stadium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Rice_University_Stadium.jpg/340px-Rice_University_Stadium.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rice_University_Stadium.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rice Stadium</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Rice participates in <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I</a> athletics and is part of <a href="/wiki/Conference_USA" title="Conference USA">Conference USA</a>. Rice was a member of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Athletic_Conference" title="Western Athletic Conference">Western Athletic Conference</a> before joining Conference USA in 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WSJ1_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-WSJ1-113">[113]</a></sup> Rice is the second-smallest school, measured by undergraduate enrollment, competing in NCAA <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_Bowl_Subdivision" title="Football Bowl Subdivision">Division I FBS</a> <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">football</a>, only ahead of <a href="/wiki/University_of_Tulsa" title="University of Tulsa">Tulsa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WSJ1_113-1"><a href="#cite_note-WSJ1-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Rice_Owls_baseball" title="Rice Owls baseball">Rice baseball team</a> won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2003_College_World_Series" title="2003 College World Series">2003 College World Series</a>, defeating <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford</a>, giving Rice its only national championship in a team sport. The victory made Rice University the smallest school in 51 years to win a national championship at the highest collegiate level of the sport. The Rice baseball team has played on campus at <a href="/wiki/Reckling_Park" title="Reckling Park">Reckling Park</a> since the 2000 season. As of 2010, the baseball team has won 14 consecutive conference championships in three different conferences: the final championship of the defunct <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Conference" title="Southwest Conference">Southwest Conference</a>, all nine championships while a member of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Athletic_Conference" title="Western Athletic Conference">Western Athletic Conference</a>, and five more championships in its first five years as a member of <a href="/wiki/Conference_USA" title="Conference USA">Conference USA</a>. Additionally, Rice's baseball team has finished third in both the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2006_College_World_Series" title="2006 College World Series">2006</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2007_College_World_Series" title="2007 College World Series">2007 College World Series</a> tournaments. Rice now has made six trips to Omaha for the CWS. In 2004, Rice became the first school ever to have three players selected in the first eight picks of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MLB_draft" title="MLB draft">MLB draft</a> when <a href="/wiki/Philip_Humber" title="Philip Humber">Philip Humber</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Niemann" title="Jeff Niemann">Jeff Niemann</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wade_Townsend" title="Wade Townsend">Wade Townsend</a> were selected third, fourth, and eighth, respectively. In 2007, <a href="/wiki/Joe_Savery" title="Joe Savery">Joe Savery</a> was selected as the 19th overall pick.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:College_football_-_Rice_Owls_vs_Texas_Longhorns.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3456" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/College_football_-_Rice_Owls_vs_Texas_Longhorns.jpg/220px-College_football_-_Rice_Owls_vs_Texas_Longhorns.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/College_football_-_Rice_Owls_vs_Texas_Longhorns.jpg/330px-College_football_-_Rice_Owls_vs_Texas_Longhorns.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/College_football_-_Rice_Owls_vs_Texas_Longhorns.jpg/440px-College_football_-_Rice_Owls_vs_Texas_Longhorns.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:College_football_-_Rice_Owls_vs_Texas_Longhorns.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Owls in a game against the <a href="/wiki/Texas_Longhorns" title="Texas Longhorns">Texas Longhorns</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2006, the football team qualified for its first bowl game since 1961, ending the second-longest bowl drought in the country at the time. On December 22, 2006, Rice played in the <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Bowl" title="New Orleans Bowl">New Orleans Bowl</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Orleans,_Louisiana" title="New Orleans, Louisiana">New Orleans, Louisiana</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Sun_Belt_Conference" title="Sun Belt Conference">Sun Belt Conference</a> champion, Troy. The Owls lost 41-17. The bowl appearance came after Rice had a 14-game losing streak from 2004–05 and went 1-10 in 2005. The streak followed an internally authorized 2003 McKinsey report that stated football alone was responsible for a $4 million deficit in 2002. Tensions remained high between the athletic department and faculty, as a few professors who chose to voice their opinion were in favor of abandoning the football program. The program success in 2006, the "Rice Renaissance," proved to be a revival of the Owl football program, quelling those tensions. <a href="/wiki/David_Bailiff" title="David Bailiff">David Bailiff</a> took over the program in 2007 and has remained head coach. <a href="/wiki/Jarett_Dillard" title="Jarett Dillard">Jarett Dillard</a> set an NCAA record in 2006 by catching a touchdown pass in 13 consecutive games and took a 15-game overall streak into the 2007 season.</p>
<p>In 2008, the football team posted a 9-3 regular season, capping off the year with a 38-14 victory over Western Michigan University in the Texas Bowl. The win over Western Michigan marked the Owls' first bowl win in 45 years.</p>
<p>Rice Stadium also serves as the performance venue for the university's <a href="/wiki/Marching_Owl_Band" title="Marching Owl Band">Marching Owl Band</a>, or "MOB." Despite its name, the MOB is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scatter_band" title="Scatter band">scatter band</a> that focuses on performing humorous skits and routines rather than traditional formation marching.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Rice_Owls_men%27s_basketball" title="Rice Owls men's basketball">Rice Owls men's basketball</a> won 10 conference titles in the former Southwest Conference (1918, 1935*, 1940, 1942*, 1943*, 1944*, 1945, 1949*, 1954*, 1970; * denotes shared title). Most recently, guard Morris Almond was drafted in the first round of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2007_NBA_Draft" title="2007 NBA Draft">2007 NBA Draft</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Utah_Jazz" title="Utah Jazz">Utah Jazz</a>. Rice recently named former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cal_Bears" title="Cal Bears">Cal Bears</a> head coach <a href="/wiki/Ben_Braun" title="Ben Braun">Ben Braun</a> as head basketball coach to succeed Willis Wilson, fired after Rice finished the 2007-2008 season with a winless (0-16) conference record and overall record of 3-27.</p>
<p>Rice has been very successful in women's sports in recent years. In 2004-05, Rice sent its women's volleyball, soccer, and basketball teams to their respective NCAA tournaments. In 2005-06, the women's soccer, basketball, and tennis teams advanced, with five individuals competing in track and field. In 2006-07, the Rice women's basketball team made the NCAA tournament, while again five Rice track and field athletes received individual NCAA berths. In 2008, the women's volleyball team again made the NCAA tournament. In 2011 the Women's Swim team won their first conference championship in the history of the university. This was an impressive feat considering they won without having a diving team.</p>
<p>Rice's mascot is <a href="/wiki/Sammy_the_Owl" title="Sammy the Owl">Sammy the Owl</a>. In previous decades, the university kept several live owls on campus in front of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lovett_College" title="Lovett College">Lovett College</a>, but this practice has been discontinued, due to public pressure over the welfare of the owls.</p>
<p>Rice also has a 12-member coed cheerleading squad and an all-female dance team, both of which perform at football and basketball games throughout the year.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Alumni.2C_faculty_and_presidents">Alumni, faculty and presidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rice_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Alumni, faculty and presidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Rice_University_people" title="List of Rice University people">List of Rice University people</a></div>
<p>As of 2011, Rice has graduated 98 classes of students consisting of 51,961 living alumni. Over 100 students at Rice have been <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fulbright_Scholars" title="Fulbright Scholars">Fulbright Scholars</a>, 20 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marshall_Scholars" title="Marshall Scholars">Marshall Scholars</a>, 25 Mellon Fellows, 12 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhodes_Scholars" title="Rhodes Scholars">Rhodes Scholars</a>, 6 Udall Scholars, and 65 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Watson_Fellowship" title="Watson Fellowship">Watson Fellows</a>, among several other honors and awards.</p>
<p>Rice's distinguished faculty and alumni consists of 3 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nobel_laureates" title="Nobel laureates">Nobel laureates</a>, 2 <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> award winners, 6 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fulbright_Scholars" title="Fulbright Scholars">Fulbright Scholars</a>, 29 Alexander von Humboldt Foundation Recipients, 8 members of the <a href="/wiki/American_Academy_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="American Academy of Arts and Sciences">American Academy of Arts and Sciences</a>, 1 member of the <a href="/wiki/American_Philosophical_Society" title="American Philosophical Society">American Philosophical Society</a>, 35 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guggenheim_Fellowships" title="Guggenheim Fellowships">Guggenheim Fellowships</a>, 17 members of the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Engineering" title="National Academy of Engineering">National Academy of Engineering</a>, 7 members of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_National_Academy_of_Sciences" title="United States National Academy of Sciences">National Academy of Sciences</a>, 5 fellows of the <a href="/wiki/National_Humanities_Center" title="National Humanities Center">National Humanities Center</a>, and 86 fellows of the <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">National Science Foundation</a>.</p>
<p>Alumni of Rice have occupied top positions in business, including <a href="/wiki/Thomas_H._Cruikshank" title="Thomas H. Cruikshank">Thomas H. Cruikshank</a>, the former CEO of <a href="/wiki/Halliburton" title="Halliburton">Halliburton</a>; <a href="/wiki/John_Doerr" title="John Doerr">John Doerr</a>, billionaire and venture capitalist; <a href="/wiki/Howard_Hughes" title="Howard Hughes">Howard Hughes</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Fred_C._Koch" title="Fred C. Koch">Fred C. Koch</a>.</p>
<p>In government and politics, Rice alumni include <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Gonzales" title="Alberto Gonzales">Alberto Gonzales</a>, former Attorney General; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charles_Duncan,_Jr." title="Charles Duncan, Jr.">Charles Duncan</a>, former Secretary of Energy; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/William_P._Hobby,_Jr." title="William P. Hobby, Jr.">William P. Hobby, Jr.</a>; <a href="/wiki/John_Kline_(politician)" title="John Kline (politician)">John Kline</a>; <a href="/wiki/George_P._Bush" title="George P. Bush">George P. Bush</a>; <a href="/wiki/Josh_Earnest" title="Josh Earnest">Josh Earnest</a>, White House Press Secretary for President Obama; <a href="/wiki/Ben_Rhodes_(White_House_staffer)" title="Ben Rhodes (White House staffer)">Ben Rhodes</a>, Deputy National Security Advisor for President Obama and <a href="/wiki/Annise_Parker" title="Annise Parker">Annise Parker</a>, the 61st Mayor of Houston.</p>
<p>Rice alumni who became prominent writers include <a href="/wiki/Larry_McMurtry" title="Larry McMurtry">Larry McMurtry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a>-winning author and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Oscar</a>-winning writer of the screenplay for <i><a href="/wiki/Brokeback_Mountain" title="Brokeback Mountain">Brokeback Mountain</a></i>; <a href="/wiki/Joyce_Carol_Oates" title="Joyce Carol Oates">Joyce Carol Oates</a>, who was once a doctoral candidate in English; <a href="/wiki/John_Graves_(author)" title="John Graves (author)">John Graves</a>, author of <i><a href="/wiki/Goodbye_to_a_River" title="Goodbye to a River">Goodbye to a River</a></i>; and <a href="/wiki/Candace_Bushnell" title="Candace Bushnell">Candace Bushnell</a>, author of <i><a href="/wiki/Sex_and_the_City_(book)" title="Sex and the City (book)">Sex and the City</a></i>, who attended for three semesters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Big_Apple_Babe:_Candace_Bushnell_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-Big_Apple_Babe:_Candace_Bushnell-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<p>Notable entrepreneurs who graduated from Rice include Tim and Karrie League, founders of the <a href="/wiki/Alamo_Drafthouse_Cinema" title="Alamo Drafthouse Cinema">Alamo Drafthouse Cinema</a> and Drafthouse Films; and Brock Wagner and Kevin Bartol, founders of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Arnold_Brewing_Company" title="Saint Arnold Brewing Company">Saint Arnold Brewing Company</a>.</p>
<p>In science and technology, Rice alumni include 14 <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> <a href="/wiki/Astronaut" title="Astronaut">astronauts</a>; <a href="/wiki/Robert_Curl" title="Robert Curl">Robert Curl</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a>-winning discoverer of <a href="/wiki/Fullerene" title="Fullerene">fullerene</a>; <a href="/wiki/Robert_Woodrow_Wilson" title="Robert Woodrow Wilson">Robert Woodrow Wilson</a>, winner of the Nobel Prize in Physics for the discovery of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cosmic_microwave_background_radiation" title="Cosmic microwave background radiation">cosmic microwave background radiation</a>; <a href="/wiki/David_Eagleman" title="David Eagleman">David Eagleman</a>, celebrity neuroscientist and NYT bestselling author; and NASA former Apollo 11 and 13 warning systems engineer and motivational speaker Jerry Woodfill.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jerry-Woodfill_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jerry-Woodfill-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>Rice athletes include <a href="/wiki/Lance_Berkman" title="Lance Berkman">Lance Berkman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bubba_Crosby" title="Bubba Crosby">Bubba Crosby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harold_Solomon" title="Harold Solomon">Harold Solomon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Ryan_(American_football)" title="Frank Ryan (American football)">Frank Ryan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Kramer" title="Tommy Kramer">Tommy Kramer</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jose_Cruz,_Jr." title="Jose Cruz, Jr.">Jose Cruz, Jr.</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/O.J._Brigance" title="O.J. Brigance">O.J. Brigance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Cingrani" title="Tony Cingrani">Tony Cingrani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Rendon" title="Anthony Rendon">Anthony Rendon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leo_Rucka" title="Leo Rucka">Leo Rucka</a>, as well as three <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympians</a>.</p>
